  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_733f9e0a-ab6e-43ca-a47e-80d1d6c2438d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/900871-i-am-about-half-way-through-the-book-and">I am about half way through the book and this character Flaco Jinenez Spanish pirate just showed up. I don&#39;t remember him from the earlier books but Jacky knows him. Could someone PLEASE tell me earlier book he was in if he was????</a>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6575298-tessa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1604208789i/6575298._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6575298-tessa">Tessa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Jacky met Flaco while sailing in the Caribbean on the <i>Emerald</i> but their meeting is not actually portrayed in any of the books. The meeting took place <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Jacky met Flaco while sailing in the Caribbean on the <i>Emerald</i> but their meeting is not actually portrayed in any of the books. The meeting took place during "Under the Jolly Roger" but this is the first book that Flaco makes an appearance in. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <span id="freeText2459129708579046372" style="display:none">Anyone else feel like the way Meyer's writes Jacky's sexuality is a getting kind of skeezy? I'm all for Jacky Faber, champion flirter but the way he writes her is coming off as increasingly male gazey. Plus most of her love interests are jackasses, like by now I know if Jacky meets a dude and he's an asshole she'll be probably by making out with him by the end of the book. :/ I think it might not come off so gross if Meyer would let her age properly. There is no way on earth it makes sense for her to only be sixteen within the timeframe of the story. If I'm guessing low and assigning one year per book (and considering how much goes down each book I really think some encompass more than a year) she ought to be nineteen at the very least by now. Also I would give alot to get rid of the attempted rape scenes she's subjected to every single book.<br /><br />With that little critique done I will say I did enjoy this book. Jacky Faber, professional mermaid! Inventor of the swimming suit and flipper finns! (I suspect the next book will feature Jacky founding modern medical science, it seems like a plausible next step after anachronistically discovering the benefits of alcohol sterilization). The series looks to be winding down now, I look forward to seeing her crowned king of all pirates (what, that has to be end. I can think of literally no profession Jacky Faber would be more intrinsically suited to). 3.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_270820895" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270820895" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270820895?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kathryn by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/447743-tyler">Tyler</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270820895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer277689383124362969">Another delightful adventure with Jacky Faber, who is now like a very dear friend to me. In this adventure, we find Jacky sent by King George to the waters off Cuba and Key West, diving for sunken Spanish treasure. I will try to avoid spoilers for both this book and for the previous books, and simply say that this was perhaps one of the most enjoyable of Jacky’s adventures because, for the most part, it was fairly cheerful. Aside from a few heart-wrenching moments (one involving a tale told by a</span>
  <span id="freeText277689383124362969" style="display:none">Another delightful adventure with Jacky Faber, who is now like a very dear friend to me. In this adventure, we find Jacky sent by King George to the waters off Cuba and Key West, diving for sunken Spanish treasure. I will try to avoid spoilers for both this book and for the previous books, and simply say that this was perhaps one of the most enjoyable of Jacky’s adventures because, for the most part, it was fairly cheerful. Aside from a few heart-wrenching moments (one involving a tale told by a freed slave, the other when Jacky watches a bullfight), it was mostly smooth sailing (pardon the pun) for Jacky this time around. The supporting cast provided many colorful and engaging moments, including the vile peacock of a Spanish officer Cisneros, and the return of the gallant and amorous Floco (Jacky’s good-natured and handsome pirate friend whom I had not met, having skipped the book he was featured in). I liked Jemima and her “Brother Rabbit” (Brer Rabbit) stories, too, though I felt the name was rather an unfortunate choice for this African-American woman, especially considering she is making pancakes in one of her first scenes. I was delighted that Jamie, Jacky’s betrothed, also features in this book in person vs. the letters I have come to know him by from previous books. He and Jacky must promise not to enter into any sort of, ahem, amorous adventures together which creates quite a lot of sexual tension, as Jacky is quite the lusty lass and Jamie is, well, a young man very eager for his wedding night. I am not sure what age these books are geared for, but I would place this one firmly in the YA category given the sexual innuendo. I enjoyed the setting, and the sunken treasure aspect gave a new twist for Jacky’s adventures. If you enjoyed the previous Jacky books, keep reading. The quality remains strong!<br /><br />If you listen to the audiobook, which I highly recommend thanks to Katherine Kellgren's marvelous reading, be sure to stay tuned after the last chapter for an interesting twenty minute interview with Kellgren and author LA Meyer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="277689383124362969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Really? Just really, stream of conscience can go too far. That and Umms in italics when she kisses someone...gross.<br/><br/>And just as far as her as a character she has become really distast</span>
  <span id="freeText16039519145070685407" style="display:none">Going through this I started to remember that there were writing flaws in the other books that I had forgotten about since I read the last book two years ago.<br />Most of it is written in the first person present which impossibly annoying because who wants to read "we are going there, we are so close. yes, we are there." Really? Just really, stream of conscience can go too far. That and Umms in italics when she kisses someone...gross.<br /><br />And just as far as her as a character she has become really distasteful, and she's not the kind of character that can get away with that. She seems to have become a Mama (like for whores) rather than the female rugged-Liberace that she was before. Now it just seems we have to listen to her vainglorious musing about her genius and successes. That and to her concerns about all the sex people around her are having.<br /><br />It's also become an insanely annoying habit of the writer take moments and remind us over and over that she was raised as an orphan, "well I wasn't raised proper." So? That's no excuse for loose morals. Oh yeah, that's another thing, she kisses every guy she sees as attractive and makes sex jokes with them (which are painful to read.) We have to listen to her inner 'struggles' over whether or not to be all over these guys or be faithful.<br /><br />She does not seem like a woman, which makes sense because the writer is a man. For instance her obsession with every man and woman she knows getting paired up and get busy so they can have tons of babies. That and her acceptance of man acting like pigs "oops, it's just male honor," when she used to have some honor herself so she would not take that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16039519145070685407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7307582732061640525">Considering my distaste with how long L.A. Meyer is dragging on about maintaining Jacky's virginity and her frustrating relationship with British Navy, I loved this book.<br/><br/>Jacky is finally reunited with her beloved Jaimy and they are nearly at the alter getting married, when Jacky is whisked away by the British Naval Intelligence to recover sunken Spanish gold. Supposedly, they are still angry that she didn't kill Napoleon when she had the chance, so her punishment is to abstain from sex until aft</span>
  <span id="freeText7307582732061640525" style="display:none">Considering my distaste with how long L.A. Meyer is dragging on about maintaining Jacky's virginity and her frustrating relationship with British Navy, I loved this book.<br /><br />Jacky is finally reunited with her beloved Jaimy and they are nearly at the alter getting married, when Jacky is whisked away by the British Naval Intelligence to recover sunken Spanish gold. Supposedly, they are still angry that she didn't kill Napoleon when she had the chance, so her punishment is to abstain from sex until after their mission is complete. Lucky for Jacky, Jaimy is allowed to help with the mission, as 3rd Mate on the Dolphin, the ship that is supposed to accompany the Nancy B in their endeavor. And so begins the adventure. Jacky gets to reunite most of her brotherhood, add another female crewmember, see a slave auction, and run into a few of her previous suitors, the Spanish pirate Flaco and Captain Richard Allen. <br /><br />There's really not much else to the story, but it was cute and we had more time with Jaimy. I am liking him a lot more and the boy has definitely grown up some. Still kinda bland though. I, myself, lust after Flaco or even Richard Allen, but Jaimy's still kinda cute.<br /><br />Overall, its a good addition, but honestly, I just want it to end. No, not really end, but I no longer want Jacky drawn to be her still intact virginity. It has dragged on way too long and I would appreciate a nice satisfying finale. But considering that there are at least 2 books after this one, I doubt it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16781824314987246976">Just as a note to start, this is one of the best books/series to listen to... Katherine Kellgren is amazing and the accents and music bring the story to life in a way you don't get from reading the print version. So... go listen to it!<br/><br/>This is one of my favorite YA series, which feels weird to say, because I normally can't stand historical fiction. I've also finally caught up to the end of the series, and now have to wait for the next book. Jacky is a phenomenal character and the sort of person I</span>
  <span id="freeText16781824314987246976" style="display:none">Just as a note to start, this is one of the best books/series to listen to... Katherine Kellgren is amazing and the accents and music bring the story to life in a way you don't get from reading the print version. So... go listen to it!<br /><br />This is one of my favorite YA series, which feels weird to say, because I normally can't stand historical fiction. I've also finally caught up to the end of the series, and now have to wait for the next book. Jacky is a phenomenal character and the sort of person I wish I was a little more like... though a little Jacky goes a long way. She's strong, tough, resourceful, and has an excellent sense of humor. However, I feel like the series is dragging just a little. This book moved fairly quickly and didn't hold me in the same way of previous adventures, particularly "In the Belly of the Bloodhound" or "Under the Jolly Roger." That being said, I will continue to read the Bloody Jack books... I like Jacky just too much to stop! And while I'm not wild about Jamie, I'd like to see a happy ending for the two of them. <br /><br />Here's looking forward to this September and "The Wake of the Lorelei Lee!"</span>

<div id="review_1166601780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166601780" />
    <a title="Mum " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1930167-mum"><img alt="Mum " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243526459p2/1930167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166601780?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mum " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mum " href="/user/show/1930167-mum">Mum </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781593164836" href="/book/show/7916695-rapture-of-the-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166601780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer154776653184072333">kindle/audio<br/><br/>Okay, if 2 stars is 'it was ok' and 3 stars is 'I liked it' then I have to fall somewhere in the middle of that.<br/><br/>**SPOILER ALERT** While I don't discuss specific plot points or give away the ending, I do mention things that happen in the book. Read on knowing you have been warned.<br/><br/>I have been a fan of this series up until now, giving books 5 star reviews that really don't deserve them on their literary merit, but because they are entertaining, hysterical quick reads that are good break</span>
  <span id="freeText154776653184072333" style="display:none">kindle/audio<br /><br />Okay, if 2 stars is 'it was ok' and 3 stars is 'I liked it' then I have to fall somewhere in the middle of that.<br /><br />**SPOILER ALERT** While I don't discuss specific plot points or give away the ending, I do mention things that happen in the book. Read on knowing you have been warned.<br /><br />I have been a fan of this series up until now, giving books 5 star reviews that really don't deserve them on their literary merit, but because they are entertaining, hysterical quick reads that are good breaks between more mature books. We all need comic relief sometimes, right? Well this one was a little on the ridiculous side even for a Bloody Jack book. In this book Jacky invents swimming fins, is the first to dive the ocean depths to retrieve treasure (seriously, with no weights she swims out of the bell and collects things and never floats up? Come on! And she recovers from an episode of decompression sickness or the bends in time to dive the next day!?), invents the bikini, becomes the first to sanitize medical equipment because she finds it reduces the chances of infection, meets Rick in Havana. That Rick. Casablanca Rick. There's more, I just can't remember it all right now.<br /><br />Anyway, as usual there are suitors a-plenty and Jacky has no qualms about leading them all on and right up to a certain point where they all must stop because she is saving herself for Jaimy. This is getting old. The plot was a little overworked here and I didn't see much point. There is a near rape. Every.Single.Book! Come on!<br /><br />I also wish that Jacky would age a bit more. If she was 18-20 I'd feel a bit better about her behavior, but a 16 year old, who for at least 2 years has been galavanting around the world breaking hearts and whatever else. I guess in the first few books I felt as if she might be developing a bit of a moral compass, but that ended. I don't need her to be a nun, just not a slut. And these books, written by a man who makes Jacky seem really gross, wiggling her bum on the lap of the pirate and letting him put his hairy face between her breasts and shake it back and forth-that has a name I think-is just creepy in a way. I'm not a total prude, so it isn't that it happens, just the way he writes it. Dirty old man creepy. And these books are supposed to be for the middle school set. Ummmm. I wouldn't let my girls read them at that age. No way.<br /><br />So. I am half-way through the series that I know has an ending because the final book was released last fall. Will I or won't I? Well, I won't for a little while anyway, then we shall see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="154776653184072333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40748625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40748625" />
    <a title="Caitlín (Ink Mage)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/995753-caitl-n-ink-mage"><img alt="Caitlín (Ink Mage)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234189508p2/995753.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Caitlín (Ink Mage)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlín (Ink Mage)" href="/user/show/995753-caitl-n-ink-mage">Caitlín (Ink Mage)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/995753-caitl-n-ink-mage?shelf=particular-favorites">particular-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/995753-caitl-n-ink-mage?shelf=nautical">nautical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer40748625&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40748625" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16659146079347845092">Okay, so where do I start? Basically with, I hope this book isn't an indication of the series going WAY. DOWN. HILL.<br/><i>Rapture</i> began with a good premise and had me expecting another rollicking adventure. But after the first 105 pages (or, parts I and II) it didn't live up to it. Yes, Jacky and Jaimy were together, but all they did was try--and fail--again and again to have "quiet moments," and Jacky told Jaimy what to do ALL THE TIME. I didn't even really like Jaimy for most of this book; the only </span>
  <span id="freeText16659146079347845092" style="display:none">Okay, so where do I start? Basically with, I hope this book isn't an indication of the series going WAY. DOWN. HILL.<br /><i>Rapture</i> began with a good premise and had me expecting another rollicking adventure. But after the first 105 pages (or, parts I and II) it didn't live up to it. Yes, Jacky and Jaimy were together, but all they did was try--and fail--again and again to have "quiet moments," and Jacky told Jaimy what to do ALL THE TIME. I didn't even really like Jaimy for most of this book; the only time I felt any genuine liking for him was when he braved the diving bell, something he feared greatly, for Jacky's sake. It was very sweet. Otherwise, simply held the place of "the most beautiful boy" with no brain.<br /><br />Secondly--which should perhaps be first--WHAT WAS WITH MR. MEYER REPEATING HIMSELF SO MANY TIMES?! I was nearly ready to scream by the end if I heard about Higgins' and his stupid towel-at-the-ready one more time. And entire sentences and explanations of various things were repeated many times--sometimes even on following pages.<br /><br />A lot of the book seemed like boring filler--<b>especially</b> the Bother/Fox/Bear/Rabbit stories, which are apparently required to appear in every single book featuring slavery and/or an old slave who imports "wisdom" to the young.<br /><br />I did like it from page 412 on, where a certain red-coated rascal appeared to save the day (and make me laugh!). I *loved* the scene with Richard Allen and the bomb--best true-to-character moment ever! It was nice, for once, that the book ended without a ton of drama in the last paragraph, but I'd almost rather have a cliffhanger because frankly I'm not all that excited for Book 8.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16659146079347845092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_723530452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/723530452" />
    <a title="Lori Twichell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24081756-lori-twichell"><img alt="Lori Twichell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379611683p2/24081756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723530452?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori Twichell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori Twichell" href="/user/show/24081756-lori-twichell">Lori Twichell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723530452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15842426233262746341">With more adventures, wild crazy schemes and just the right amount of danger, the Rapture of the Deep continues the grand tradition of the Bloody Jack series. As with the previous books, Jacky’s danger level rises considerably and though targeted to 8th grade and up, there are some heavy situations in here that aren’t necessarily appropriate for younger teens. Pretty much the same warning I’ve given throughout the other books applies. Jacky’s adventures aren’t simple, light or easy. She ends up </span>
  <span id="freeText15842426233262746341" style="display:none">With more adventures, wild crazy schemes and just the right amount of danger, the Rapture of the Deep continues the grand tradition of the Bloody Jack series. As with the previous books, Jacky’s danger level rises considerably and though targeted to 8th grade and up, there are some heavy situations in here that aren’t necessarily appropriate for younger teens. Pretty much the same warning I’ve given throughout the other books applies. Jacky’s adventures aren’t simple, light or easy. She ends up in danger and often, in highly violent or even sexual situations.<br /><br />Even better is the audio version of the book – with Jacky’s adventures acted out in spectacular detail. With songs, beautiful voices and exceptional acting, this is the best audio book series that I have ever had the opportunity to experience. I never cease to be impressed with the magnitude of the production. When I have considered audiobooks in the past, most of the time it’s simple reading. There may be some voices, but you can always tell that it’s the same actor. That is not the case with this series. As I was listening, I was completely caught up in the audio version of Jacky’s tales. I found myself listening all the time! I didn’t want to stop.<br /><br />Next stop: The Wake of the Lorelei Lee!<br /><br /><br />Review copy provided by the publisher and Listen and Live Audio. Thank you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15842426233262746341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14845296598372809443">Meyer never fails to deliver an amazing tale of love, adventure, friendship, and the luck of a certain impulsive maiden.<br/><br/>The momment a good friend had thrusted the town library's battered copy of Bloody Jack into my reluctant hands, and commanded me to read the first chapter, I was spellbound.<br/><br/>In a little over a week, I had flashed through the available following books.   <span id="freeText14845296598372809443" style="display:none">Meyer never fails to deliver an amazing tale of love, adventure, friendship, and the luck of a certain impulsive maiden.<br /><br />The momment a good friend had thrusted the town library's battered copy of Bloody Jack into my reluctant hands, and commanded me to read the first chapter, I was spellbound.<br /><br />In a little over a week, I had flashed through the available following books. I ended today, on Rapture of the Deep, starving for the next installment.<br /><br />Readers will find this series heartwarming. I for one found the adventures Jacky Faber an elegant mix of history, romance, and adventure, with L.A. Meyer's unique prose adding to the novelty of the action.<br /><br />If you have yet to pick up the books, I recommend you harden your sea legs, and hop on, for Miss Faber is about to take you on a journey unlike any other.</span>

Readers will enjoy visiting ports in London, Boston and Havana with Jacky and her crew.This is the 7th in the Bloody Jack Adventures series.</span>

<div id="review_2164509142" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164509142" />
    <a title="Clare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4927816-clare"><img alt="Clare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302422936p2/4927816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164509142?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare" href="/user/show/4927816-clare">Clare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2164509142&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164509142" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11774739830723819225">I really love this series.<br/><br/><br/>It's got a clever female protagonist, and she does many different things -in many different places. The variety makes the series a lot of fun.<br/><br/><br/>I especially recommend the Audiobooks. The narrator, Katherine Kellgren, was incredibly talented and fun to listen to. <br/><br/><br/>However, now that I've gotten to the second half of the series, there are a few things about Jacky that have become frustrating. <br/><br/><br/>(Spoiler)<br/><br/><br/><br/>The main character is quite young -in the books I think she starts out at 1</span>
  <span id="freeText11774739830723819225" style="display:none">I really love this series.<br /><br /><br />It's got a clever female protagonist, and she does many different things -in many different places. The variety makes the series a lot of fun.<br /><br /><br />I especially recommend the Audiobooks. The narrator, Katherine Kellgren, was incredibly talented and fun to listen to. <br /><br /><br />However, now that I've gotten to the second half of the series, there are a few things about Jacky that have become frustrating. <br /><br /><br />(Spoiler)<br /><br /><br /><br />The main character is quite young -in the books I think she starts out at 12 yo, and by the end she's 19... So much of her behavior could possibly be attributed to her youth and immaturity? Except at that time girls in their teens did get married quite frequently... I don't know how realistic it is.   Despite her constant flotation and her tendency to be a bit of a Mary Sue )she seems to be really good at every single thing that she does, so much better than everyone else,) the stories are still fun and original.<br /><br /><br />Mr Meyer created an intelligent, spirited and funny protagonist. However she's also a lot of things aren't great-which does make her more well-rounded because real people have lots of faults. It's just that she has a couple of repeated behaviors that have slowly made me start to not like her as much. For example she has fiance that she has been repeatedly trying to get married to, but things keep happening to stop it. We are told that she really loves Jamie, and it does seem like her and Jamie are a good match. But whenever he's not there she's sitting in other men's laps and kissing them, constantly. Also, at times it seems like the author is trying to make us feel that Jamie's jealousy is irrational, but he's not just someone she's dating or even courting. He's her fiance. I know if I was Jamie I would not have lasted nearly as long as he did. It makes her seem exceptionally selfish, even though we're constantly being told that she'd do anything for her friends - it seems more that she also does whatever she wants despite constantly receiving really good advice.<br /><br />Despite the constant Jamie torturing/playing with other men (and being kind of mean about it sometimes) the books are still wonderful. Katherine Kellgren was incredibly, incredibly talented. Her narration is funny and spirited.  She must have been an excellent actor because all of the characters have unique voices that are consistent throughout all the books and she infuses an unbelievable amount of emotion into the stories. Also, since our lead character is a bit of a Mary Sue who can do almost everything… she's also supposed to be very musical &amp; love entertaining. Katherine Kellgren does an incredible job with the songs in the stories. I'm really really glad I didn't read this in a hardcover because I think the audiobooks have got to be a thousand times better just because of how much emotion, music, and fun are woven into the audio version. There were multiple times I wondered if it was possible to just listen to the songs later!<br /><br /><br />I really would recommend this series, despite Jackie's constant flirtations. It does a wonderful job of putting you into the time period and the various situations that she gets herself into - especially the really vivid descriptions of shipboard life in the 1800s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11774739830723819225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3643864740?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/5087312-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3643864740&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3643864740" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7386343474696489221">Cw: battle scenes between several ships; pistol fights; blood and gore; rooster fighting as sport, gambling; characters free diving in the open ocean; one scene of a character getting the bends after diving; a diving bell that may be considered claustrophobic; graphic attempted sexual assault; period-typical slurs against women, Black and Indigenous people; one head injury; crocodile attacks; whipping as punishment; sexual situations and mentions of sexuality; several scenes of surgery/medical c</span>
  <span id="freeText7386343474696489221" style="display:none">Cw: battle scenes between several ships; pistol fights; blood and gore; rooster fighting as sport, gambling; characters free diving in the open ocean; one scene of a character getting the bends after diving; a diving bell that may be considered claustrophobic; graphic attempted sexual assault; period-typical slurs against women, Black and Indigenous people; one head injury; crocodile attacks; whipping as punishment; sexual situations and mentions of sexuality; several scenes of surgery/medical care of battle wounds, including placing of stitches.<br /><br />I really should have been doing content warnings for all of these because be assured, shit goes down in each of these books, but they're so damn long that I always forget everything by the end. I want to specifically point out the sexual assault scene in this book, as it is slightly more graphic than in past installments; as always, the language is a bit vague so it's not super super graphic, but it is certainly enough to paint a distressing picture. <br /><br />This book is a nice return to the roots of the series after the previous installment. We are once again at sea, and several well-liked characters return. The addition of Capitan Flaco Jimenez is the only real complaint I have about this book; we are suddenly introduced to another old flame from Jacky's time on the Emerald, a Spanish pirate with whom she would pillage. This is the first time a character has been retroactively introduced, so that's a little strange, though in the 3rd book we did sort of skim over the summer of 1804(?) so it's not as though it doesn't fit in. It does add a layer of complication to Jacky's claim that she was only ever a privateer, which judging by some of the behavior on the Werewolf and the Emerald was already on thin ice. Her claims of never being a pirate are sort of harder to believe with this addition of literally pillaging with a literal pirate (who is also of a nationality that is at war with the Crown), but I digress. <br />I will also note that it felt sort of strange to have Jacky not think cock fighting is cruel, but maybe there's a metaphor for herself somewhere in there? And the extended sequences of Jemimah telling slave folk tales didn't seem to have any import on the plot (no parallels, lessons, or anything), so I'm not sure why they are included. I'm white so I can't really say anything about whether or not Jemimah's character is a stereotype, but these scenes felt sort of unnecessarily extended at least.<br /><br />Everything else is a fun time here. Also it's getting even hornier, like notably so, especially within Jaimy's pov. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8470767791129158675">TW for s*x*al as*a*lt and r**e<br/><br/>4.75/5<br/><br/>I loved this book, but it does have a few flaws that keep it from being a 5 star read. First of all, I loved that this book got us back into the water and spent the majority of its time on ships rather than on land. However, I did love the port visits that Jacky and her crew made. Things that bring this book down to a 4.75 include once again the cheating on Jaimy and the near s*x*al as*a*lt that happens in pretty much every book in this series. I get that this</span>
  <span id="freeText8470767791129158675" style="display:none">TW for s*x*al as*a*lt and r**e<br /><br />4.75/5<br /><br />I loved this book, but it does have a few flaws that keep it from being a 5 star read. First of all, I loved that this book got us back into the water and spent the majority of its time on ships rather than on land. However, I did love the port visits that Jacky and her crew made. Things that bring this book down to a 4.75 include once again the cheating on Jaimy and the near s*x*al as*a*lt that happens in pretty much every book in this series. I get that this is probably something that happened during this time period, but jeez I don't want to read about it--especially not multiple times in every book. I also detested the stories that Jemimah was telling the kids throughout the book. This felt totally unnecessary and I found it really difficult to get through these parts. Also there was really no lesson that anyone learned from them. Just the one time when Jemimah ran up to Jacky and said 'What would brother rabbit do'. They served no purpose. This was definitely not my favorite book of the series, but it had some really good scenes in it and I enjoyed the read. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The only thing that really lacked was the ending. We were gearing up for the big battle and there were only about 20 pages left in the book. So although the battle was great and everything I could have wanted, the aftermath is where I feel like there could have been more. It felt like the book just kind of ended in a weird place because we didn't have some dramatic scene where Jacky almost gets to be with Jaimy but then something else gets in the way. Which I'm glad that didn't happen because I was getting pretty tired of it. But still, the ending just didn't feel right.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=little-known-books-that-are-great">little-known-books-that-are-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=book-club-recommendations">book-club-recommendations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=books-i-wish-my-friends-would-read">books-i-wish-my-friends-would-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=women-who-kick-ass-and-take-names">women-who-kick-ass-and-take-names</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40706083-herman?shelf=ya-young-adults">ya-young-adults</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548185143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1523887698159932826">Jacky's adventures on the Spanish Main, and being the first deep sea diver using an early version of a diving bell. <br/><br/>As a straight up adventure it was OK, but as a Jacky Faber adventure it just didn’t reach the high bar that the earlier books had achieved. The enemy this time is the Spanish instead of the French and of course always the evil plotters of the English intelligent service are back and after honor and her life once again. This formula has been used a number of times by this author and</span>
  <span id="freeText1523887698159932826" style="display:none">Jacky's adventures on the Spanish Main, and being the first deep sea diver using an early version of a diving bell. <br /><br />As a straight up adventure it was OK, but as a Jacky Faber adventure it just didn’t reach the high bar that the earlier books had achieved. The enemy this time is the Spanish instead of the French and of course always the evil plotters of the English intelligent service are back and after honor and her life once again. This formula has been used a number of times by this author and it’s starting to become predictable bringing about some disappointment in me, with my skyhigh expectations. We are also introduced to a new male rogue character this red devil called Flaco, I don’t recall those Mediterranean adventures that are alluded to as their backstory but it must be difficult to write an adventure series as good as this one and not make a few mistakes with the timeline. I mean it would have been nice to know the history of this pirate captain back about book three under the Jolly Roger where I think they first met. Can’t recall reading that encounter but maybe I’m wrong hard to believe I’m on book seven in this series. A series that holds my interest this long is pretty good. Anyway another couple of villains bite the dust. Jacky escapes off to her next adventure riding high having spent half of this book wearing the first bikini (I think) and another starkers moment that will undoubtedly go down in naval lore. So while I enjoyed the book it’s just not in the same league as the others in this series so going give it a three stars this time. <br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309765853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14606214702460885923">Bloody Jack is one of my absolute favorite YA series. It's exciting, it's fun, it's always an adventure—I adore it. I've been reading the remaining books in the series slowly, knowing that there will be no more Jacky or any other kind of books from this author. RIP, Mr. Meyer.<br/><br/>RAPTURE OF THE DEEP is another fun adventure for Jacky. This time, she's (reluctantly) on another mission for Naval Intelligence. She's tasked with finding a wrecked Spanish ship and bringing home its treasure to fill King </span>
  <span id="freeText14606214702460885923" style="display:none">Bloody Jack is one of my absolute favorite YA series. It's exciting, it's fun, it's always an adventure—I adore it. I've been reading the remaining books in the series slowly, knowing that there will be no more Jacky or any other kind of books from this author. RIP, Mr. Meyer.<br /><br />RAPTURE OF THE DEEP is another fun adventure for Jacky. This time, she's (reluctantly) on another mission for Naval Intelligence. She's tasked with finding a wrecked Spanish ship and bringing home its treasure to fill King George's coffers. Jacky's got a nose for gold that rarely leads her astray. She's also got a knack for finding trouble wherever she goes—and this time is no exception.<br /><br />This is another entertaining installment in a funny, always enjoyable series starring an unforgettable heroine. Jacky Faber is one of a kind. Any time I need a pick-me-up read, I grab one starring this "salty sailor girl"—she never fails me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1028700746748951612">I am continuing to listen to the exploits of Jacky Faber with my group; one person nearing the last book, one lucky friend in the midst of "rapture" and one gal just ahead on book 8. At the end of "rapture" (HA), there was an interview with the author and the voice artist. It was really enjoyable! These people are so smart and talented, no wonder we are very entertained. It isn't realistic or high brow reading but it is based on historical facts so I actually do learn a little something, which i</span>
  <span id="freeText1028700746748951612" style="display:none">I am continuing to listen to the exploits of Jacky Faber with my group; one person nearing the last book, one lucky friend in the midst of "rapture" and one gal just ahead on book 8. At the end of "rapture" (HA), there was an interview with the author and the voice artist. It was really enjoyable! These people are so smart and talented, no wonder we are very entertained. It isn't realistic or high brow reading but it is based on historical facts so I actually do learn a little something, which is essential for my enjoyment. Did your mind just go back to "rapture" when I said enjoyment? <br />I do miss reading but enjoy discussing these audio books with my buddies. I am going to read some self-help books and continue to listen to Jacky Faber when I can. Maybe I will read how to declutter and listen while I clean? Talk about a rapturous thought! Rapture of the deep basement: Being an account of the further neurosis of Meredith Fry, hoarder, social media junkie, dog enabler. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jDR1xY8Sph5MMgVtwdT9qMA9HS2X45A8PkYzKZqyBX8e8sbHj5LZqvUO81KDWX/MEYbGjiftZB3kOd6sIj3wJg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('waSiLjCqIM94Z4qkrzV3YQg3K4eNIWGW8RYbA9XtRm1TYhEsMCpfe8FbfJvtuPUF2YzwJD0vlbcrafaGbWKzNA==')})
  }

The hi<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1169113908431373\" style=\"display:none\">Route 312 is the Chinese Route 66. It flows three thousand miles from east to west, passing through the factory towns of the coastal areas, through the rural heart of China, then up into the Gobi Desert, where it merges with the Old Silk Road. The highway witnesses every part of the social and economic revolution that is turning China upside down.In this utterly surprising and deeply personal book, acclaimed National Public Radio reporter Rob Gifford, a fluent Mandarin speaker, takes the dramatic journey along Route 312 from its start in the boomtown of Shanghai to its end on the border with Kazakhstan. Gifford reveals the rich mosaic of modern Chinese life in all its contradictions, as he poses the crucial questions that all of us are asking about China: Will it really be the next global superpower? Is it as solid and as powerful as it looks from the outside? And who are the ordinary Chinese people, to whom the twenty-first century is supposed to belong? Gifford is not alone on his journey. The largest migration in human history is taking place along highways such as Route 312, as tens of millions of people leave their homes in search of work. He sees signs of the booming urban economy everywhere, but he also uncovers many of the country’s frailties, and some of the deep-seated problems that could derail China’s rise. The whole compelling adventure is told through the cast of colorful characters Gifford meets: garrulous talk-show hosts and ambitious yuppies, impoverished peasants and tragic prostitutes, cell-phone salesmen, AIDS patients, and Tibetan monks. He rides with members of a Shanghai jeep club, hitchhikes across the Gobi desert, and sings karaoke with migrant workers at truck stops along the way.As he recounts his travels along Route 312, Rob Gifford gives a face to what has historically, for Westerners, been a faceless country and breathes life into a nation that is so often reduced to economic statistics. Finally, he sounds a warning that all is not well in the Chinese heartlands, that serious problems lie ahead, and that the future of the West has become inextricably linked with the fate of 1.3 billion Chinese people.“Informative, delightful, and powerfully moving . . . Rob Gifford’s acute powers of observation, his sense of humor and adventure, and his determination to explore the wrenching dilemmas of China’s explosive development open readers’ eyes and reward their minds.” –Robert A. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15576296262992771961">Louis A. Meyer is best known as the author of the Bloody Jack novels. He was also a painter and the author of two children's picture books, and he and his wife owned an art gallery called Clair de Loon in Bar Harbor.<br/><br/>Louis A. Meyer passed away on July 29, 2014 from refractory Hodgkin’s Lymphoma. His final Jacky Faber book, Wild Rover No More, was published posthumously in September that year.</span>
